text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_highland_climate" title="Subtropical highland climate">(Cwb) <b>Subtropical highland</b>, dry winter</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C6FF4E; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">(Cfa) Subtropical humid summer (no dry)</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF00FE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">(Dsa) Continental hot summer</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C600C7; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">(Dsb) Continental warm summer</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5A77DB; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">(Dwb) Continental dry winter</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #4C51B5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">(Dwc) Contin subarctic, dry winter</a></div></div></div></div></div>\n<p>The climate of this vast region varies considerably from area to area from tropical monsoon in the south to temperate in the north. The variety is influenced by not only the altitude, but also by factors such as proximity to the sea coast and the seasonal impact of the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoons</a>. Southern parts are mostly hot in summers and receive rain during monsoon periods. The northern belt of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_plain" title="Indo-Gangetic plain">Indo-Gangetic plains</a> also is hot in summer, but cooler in winter. The mountainous north is colder and receives snowfall at higher altitudes of Himalayan ranges.\n</p><p>As the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a> block the north-Asian bitter cold winds, the temperatures are considerably moderate in the plains down below. For most part, the climate of the region is called the <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">Monsoon</a> climate, which keeps the region humid during summer and dry during winter, and favours the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Jute" title="Jute">jute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, and various vegetables in this region.\n</p><p>South Asia is largely divided into four broad climate zones:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-olive1_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-olive1-169">[165]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The northern Indian edge and northern Pakistani uplands have a dry subtropical <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a></li>\n<li>The far south of India and southwest Sri Lanka have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equatorial_climate" title="Equatorial climate">equatorial climate</a></li>\n<li>Most of the peninsula have a tropical climate with variations:\n<ul><li>Hot <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical</a> climate in northwest India</li>\n<li>Cool winter hot <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> in Bangladesh</li>\n<li>Tropical <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> in the center</li></ul></li>\n<li>The Himalayas have an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">Alpine climate</a></li></ul>\n<p>Maximum relative humidity of over 80% has been recorded in <a href="/wiki/Khasi_and_Jaintia_Hills" title="Khasi and Jaintia Hills">Khasi and Jaintia Hills</a> and Sri Lanka, while the area adjustment to Pakistan and western India records lower than 20%&#8211;30%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-olive1_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-olive1-169">[165]</a></sup> Climate of South Asia is largely characterized by <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoons</a>. South Asia depends critically on monsoon rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[166]</a></sup> Two monsoon systems exist in the region:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[167]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The summer monsoon: Wind blows from southwest to most of parts of the region. It accounts for 70%&#8211;90% of the annual precipitation.</li>\n<li>The winter monsoon: Wind blows from northeast. Dominant in Sri Lanka and Maldives.</li></ul>\n<p>The warmest period of the year precedes the monsoon season (March to mid June). In the summer the low pressures are centered over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus-Gangetic_Plain" title="Indus-Gangetic Plain">Indus-Gangetic Plain</a> and high wind from the Indian Ocean blows towards the center. The monsoons are second coolest season of the year because of high humidity and cloud covering. But, at the beginning of June the jetstreams vanish above the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Plateau" title="Tibetan Plateau">Tibetan Plateau</a>, low pressure over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indus_Valley" title="Indus Valley">Indus Valley</a> deepens and the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a> (ITCZ) moves in. The change is violent. Moderately vigorous monsoon depressions form in the Bay of Bengal and make landfall from June to September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-olive1_169-2"><a href="#cite_note-olive1-169">[165]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistical_data">Statistical data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The population of South Asia is about 1.749 billion which makes it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_continents_by_population#Regional_and_continental_(sub)totals_in_2013" title="List of continents by population">most populated region</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[178]</a></sup> It is socially very mixed, consisting of many language groups and religions, and social practices in one region that are vastly different from those in another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[179]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_urban_areas">Largest urban areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Largest urban areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>South Asia is home to some of the most populated cities in the world. <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a> are four of the world\'s largest megacities.\n</p>\n<table class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_South_Asia" title="Languages of South Asia">Languages of South Asia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="695" data-file-width="637" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg/250px-South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg/375px-South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg/500px-South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Asian_Language_Families.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethno-linguistic distribution map of South Asia.</div></div></div>\n<p>There are numerous languages in South Asia. The spoken languages of the region are largely based on geography and shared across religious boundaries, but the written script is sharply divided by religious boundaries. In particular, Muslims of South Asia such as in Afghanistan and Pakistan use the Arabic alphabet and Persian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasta%CA%BFl%C4%ABq_script" title="Nasta&#703;l&#299;q script">Nastaliq</a>. Till 1971, Muslim Bangladesh (then known as East Pakistan) too mandated only the Nastaliq script, but thereafter has adopted regional scripts and particularly Bengali. Non-Muslims of South Asia, and some Muslims in India, on the other hand use their traditional ancient heritage scripts such as those derived from <a href="/wiki/Brahmi_script" title="Brahmi script">Brahmi script</a> for Indo-European languages and non-Brahmi scripts for <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian languages</a> and others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kachru122_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-kachru122-187">[183]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nagari_script" title="Nagari script">Nagari script</a> has been the <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i> of the traditional South Asian scripts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-george_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-george-188">[184]</a></sup> The Devanagari script is used for over 120 South Asian languages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devasilusa_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-devasilusa-189">[185]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindi_language" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[186]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pali_language" title="Pali language">Pali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konkani_language" title="Konkani language">Konkani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bodo_language" title="Bodo language">Bodo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_language" title="Sindhi language">Sindhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">Maithili</a> among other languages and dialects, making it one of the most used and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_writing_systems_by_adoption" title="List of writing systems by adoption">adopted writing systems</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[187]</a></sup> The Devanagari script is also used for classical Sanskrit texts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devasilusa_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-devasilusa-189">[185]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest spoken language in this region is <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, followed by Bengali, Tamil, Telugu, Marathi, Gujarati and Punjabi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kachru122_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-kachru122-187">[183]</a></sup> In the modern era, new syncretic languages developed in the region such as <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> that is used by Muslim community of northern south Asia (particularly Pakistan and northern states of India).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[188]</a></sup> The Punjabi language spans three religions: Islam, Hinduism and Sikhism. The spoken language is similar, but it is written in three scripts. The Sikh use <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gurmukhi_alphabet" title="Gurmukhi alphabet">Gurmukhi alphabet</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> Punjabis in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> use the Nastaliq script, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> Punjabis in India use the Gurmukhi or <a href="/wiki/N%C4%81gar%C4%AB_script" title="N&#257;gar&#299; script">N&#257;gar&#299; script</a>. The Gurmukhi and Nagari scripts are distinct but close in their structure, but the Persian Nastaliq script is very different.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bright1996p395_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bright1996p395-193">[189]</a></sup>\n</p><p>English, with British spelling, is commonly used in urban areas and is a major economic <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of South Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[190]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_India" title="Hinduism in India">Hinduism in India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_South_Asia" title="Islam in South Asia">Islam in South Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_India" title="Christianity in India">Christianity in India</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prevailing_world_religions_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Prevailing_world_religions_map.png/300px-Prevailing_world_religions_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Prevailing_world_religions_map.png/450px-Prevailing_world_religions_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Prevailing_world_religions_map.png/600px-Prevailing_world_religions_map.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prevailing_world_religions_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of <a href="/wiki/List_of_religious_populations" title="List of religious populations">major denominations and religions of the world</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2010, South Asia had the world\'s largest population of <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhs" title="Sikhs">Sikhs</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewforum.org_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-pewforum.org-9">[9]</a></sup> about 510 million <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewforum.org_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-pewforum.org-9">[9]</a></sup> as well as over 25 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhists" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a> and 35 million <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pew_Research_2012_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Research_2012-11">[11]</a></sup> Hindus make up about 68 percent or about 900 million and Muslims at 31 percent or 510 million of the overall South Asia population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[191]</a></sup> while Buddhists, Jains, Christians and Sikhs constitute most of the rest. The Hindus, Buddhists, Jains, Sikhs and Christians are concentrated in India, Nepal, Sri Lanka and Bhutan, while the Muslims are concentrated in Afghanistan (99%), Bangladesh (90%), Pakistan (96%) and Maldives (100%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewforum.org_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-pewforum.org-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Indian_religions" title="Indian religions">Indian religions</a> are the religions that originated in the India; namely <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB-196">[192]</a></sup> The Indian religions are distinct yet share terminology, concepts, goals and ideas, and from South Asia spread into East Asia and southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB_196-1"><a href="#cite_note-EB-196">[192]</a></sup> Early Christianity and Islam were introduced into coastal regions of South Asia by merchants who settled among the local populations. Later <a href="/wiki/Sindh" title="Sindh">Sindh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balochistan_(Pakistan)" title="Balochistan (Pakistan)">Balochistan</a>, and parts of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punjab_region" title="Punjab region">Punjab region</a> saw conquest by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ummayad" title="Ummayad">Arab caliphates</a> along with an influx of Muslims from Persia and Central Asia, which resulted in spread of both Shia and Sunni Islam in parts of northwestern region of South Asia. Subsequently, under the influence of Muslim rulers of the Islamic sultanates and the Mughal Empire, Islam spread in South Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[194]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Afghanistan" title="Religion in Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AfgCIA_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-AfgCIA-199">[195]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>Islam (99%), Hinduism, Sikhism and Christianity (1%)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bangladesh" title="Religion in Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a><sup class="reference" Hinduism (25%)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_India" title="Religion in India">India</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndCIA_201-1"><a (9.71%), Christianity (7.45%).\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Afghanistan" title="Religion in Afghanistan">Religion in Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bangladesh" title="Religion in Bangladesh">Religion in Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bhutan" title="Religion in href="/wiki/Religion_in_Pakistan" title="Religion in Pakistan">Religion in Pakistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Sri_Lanka" title="Religion in Sri Lanka">Religion in Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Afghanistan" title="Economy of Afghanistan">Economy of Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bangladesh" title="Economy of Bangladesh">Economy of Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_India" title="Economy of India">Economy of India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Nepal" title="Economy of Nepal">Economy of Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Pakistan" title="Economy of Pakistan">Economy of Pakistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Economy of Sri Lanka">Economy of Sri Lanka</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SAARC.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SAARC.PNG/300px-SAARC.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SAARC.PNG/450px-SAARC.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SAARC.PNG/600px-SAARC.PNG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SAARC.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries under the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Free_Trade_Area" title="South Asian Free Trade Area">South Asian Free Trade Area</a></div></div></div>\n<p>India is the largest and fastest growing economy in the region (US$2.957 trillion) and makes up almost 85% of the South Asian economy; it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">world\'s 7th largest</a> in nominal terms and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">3rd largest</a> by purchasing power adjusted exchange rates (US$8.020 trillion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMF_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-IMF-2">[2]</a></sup> India is the only member of powerful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" title="G-20 major economies">G-20 major economies</a> and <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a> from the region. It is the fastest growing major economy in the world and one of the world\'s fastest registering a growth of 7.3% in FY 2014&#8211;15.\nPakistan has the next largest economy($304.3 billion) and the 5th highest GDP per capita in the region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[205]</a></sup> followed by Bangladesh and then by <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> which has the 2nd highest per capita and is the 4th largest economy in the region. According to a <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> report in 2015, driven by a strong expansion in India, coupled with favorable oil prices, from the last quarter of 2014 South Asia become the fastest-growing region in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[206]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Major Market stock exchanges in the region are <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Stock_Exchange" title="Bombay Stock Exchange">Bombay Stock Exchange</a> (BSE) with market Capitalization of $2.298 trillion (<a href="/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges" title="List of stock exchanges">11th largest in the world</a>), <a href="/wiki/National_Stock_Exchange_of_India" title="National Stock Exchange of India">National Stock Exchange of India</a> (NSE) with market capitalization of $2.273 trillion (<a href="/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges" title="List of stock exchanges">12th largest in the world</a>), Dhaka Stock Exchange (DSE)  and  <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Stock_Exchange" title="Pakistan Stock Exchange">Pakistan Stock Exchange</a> (PSX) with market capitalization of $72 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[207]</a></sup>\nEconomic data is sourced from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, current as of April 2017, and is given in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_dollars" title="US dollars">US dollars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-212">[208]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#ececec;">\n<th><a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">Country</a><br/><sup billion\n</td>\n<td>$3,930\n</td>\n<td>4.5%\n</td>\n<td>5.8%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_nutrition">Health and nutrition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health and nutrition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">\n</th>\n<th>Afghanistan</th>\n<th>Bangladesh</th>\n<th>Bhutan</th>\n<th>India</th>\n<th>Maldives</th>\n<th>Nepal</th>\n<th>Pakistan</th>\n<th>Sri Lanka\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">Population undernourished (2015)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fao.org_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-fao.org-215">[211]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>26.8%</td>\n<td>16.4%</td>\n<td>N/A</td>\n<td>15.2%</td>\n<td>5.2%</td>\n<td>7.8%</td>\n<td>22%</td>\n<td>22%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">Population below poverty line (CIA Factbook)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Factbook-216">[212]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>35.8%</td>\n<td>31.5%</td>\n<td>12%</td>\n<td>29.8%</td>\n<td>16%</td>\n<td>25.2%</td>\n<td>22.3%</td>\n<td>8.9%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>According to WHO, South Asia is home to two out of the three countries in the world still affected by polio, Pakistan and Afghanistan, with 306 &amp; 28 polio cases registered in 2014 respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[213]</a></sup> Attempts to eradicate polio have been badly hit by opposition from militants in both countries, who say the program is cover to spy on their operations. Their attacks on immunization teams have claimed 78 lives since December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[214]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the World Bank\'s 2011 report, based on 2005 ICP PPP, about 24.6% of the South Asian population falls below the international poverty line of $1.25/day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[215]</a></sup> Afghanistan and Bangladesh rank the highest, with 30.6% and 43.3% of their respective populations below the poverty line. Bhutan, Maldives and Sri Lanka have the lowest number of people below the poverty line, with 2.4%, 1.5% and 4.1% respectively. India has lifted the most people in the region above the poverty line between 2008 and 2011, around 140 million. As of 2011, 21.9% of India\'s population lives below the poverty line, compared to 41.6% in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[217]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimates that <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> is one of the highest ranking countries in the world for the number of children suffering from <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a>. The prevalence of underweight children in India is among the highest in the world, and is nearly double that of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub_Saharan_Africa" title="Sub Saharan Africa">Sub Saharan Africa</a> with dire consequences for mobility, mortality, productivity and economic growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[218]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the World Bank, 70% of the South Asian population and about 75% of South Asia\'s poor live in rural areas and most rely on agriculture for their livelihood<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[219]</a></sup> according to the UN\'s Food and Agricultural Organisation. In 2015, approximately 281 million people in the region were malnourished. The report says that Nepal reached both the WFS target as well as MDG and is moving towards bringing down the number of undernourished people to less than 5% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fao.org_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-fao.org-215">[211]</a></sup> Bangladesh reached the MDG target with the National Food Policy framework&#160;&#8211; with only 16.5% of the population undernourished. In India, the malnourished comprise just over 15 percent of the population. While the number of malnourished people in neighborhood has shown a decline over the last 25 years, the number of under-nourished in Pakistan displays an upward trend.There were 28.7 million hungry in Pakistan in the 1990s&#160;&#8211; a number that has steadily increased to 41.3 million in 2015 with 22% of the population malnourished. Approximately 194.6 million people are undernourished in India, which accounts for the highest number of people suffering from hunger in any single country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fao.org_215-2"><a href="#cite_note-fao.org-215">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[220]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2006 report stated "the low status of women in South Asian countries and their lack of nutritional knowledge are important determinants of high prevalence of underweight children in the region". Corruption and the lack of initiative on the part of the government has been one of the major problems associated with nutrition in India. Illiteracy in villages has been found to be one of the major issues that need more government attention. The report mentioned that although there has been a reduction in malnutrition due to the <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> in South Asia, there is concern that South Asia has "inadequate feeding and caring practices for young children".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-southasiahunger_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-southasiahunger-225">[221]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote width="50"/></a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[224]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buzan2004_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-Buzan2004-229">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solomon_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Solomon-230">[226]</a></sup> are the dominant political powers in the region. India is by far the largest country in the area covering around three-fourths the land area of the South Asian region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> India has the largest population of around three times the combined population of the 6 other countries in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[227]</a></sup> India is also the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[228]</a></sup> India\'s annual defence budget for 2013&#8211;14 is $39.2 billion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[229]</a></sup> which is equal to the whole Pakistan\'s Federal budget of $39.3 billion for 2014&#8211;15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[230]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bangladesh is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[231]</a></sup> Bangladesh also stands out as one of the few Muslim-majority democracies. "It is a moderate and generally secular and tolerant &#8212; though sometimes this is getting stretched at the moment &#8212; alternative to <a href="/wiki/Violent_extremism" title="Violent extremism">violent extremism</a> in a very troubled part of the world", said <a href="/wiki/Dan_Mozena" title="Dan Mozena">Dan Mozena</a>, the U.S. ambassador to <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>. Although Bangladesh\'s legal code is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secular" title="Secular">secular</a>, more citizens are embracing a conservative version of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, with some pushing for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sharia_law" title="Sharia law">sharia law</a>, analysts say. Experts say that the rise in conservatism reflects the influence of foreign-financed Islamic charities and the more austere version of Islam brought home by migrant workers in <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[232]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Diplomacy among the countries of South Asia has been mainly driven by populist <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">politics</a>, with the centre-stage taken by <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>-<a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> conflict ever since their independence in 1947, and then the creation of Bangladesh under tense circumstances in 1971. During the height of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_war" title="Cold war">Cold war</a>, the elite political leaders of Pakistan aligned with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a>, while India played crucial <a href="/wiki/India_and_the_Non-Aligned_Movement" title="India and the Non-Aligned Movement">role</a> in forming the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and while maintaining goodwill relations with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics" title="Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">USSR</a>.\n</p><p>Pakistan\'s governance is one of the most conflicted in the region. The military rule and the unstable government in Pakistan has become a concern for the South Asian region. In <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a>, the governance has struggled to come in the side of democracy and it only showed signs in the recent past, basically in the 21st century, to support the democratic system. The political situation in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> has been dominated by an increasingly assertive <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_people" title="Sinhalese people">Sinhalese</a> nationalism, and the emergence of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamil_people" title="Sri Lankan Tamil people">Tamil</a> separatist movement under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LTTE" title="LTTE">LTTE</a>, which was suppressed in May 2009. <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>\'s politics is dominated by a military <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">Junta</a>, which has sidelined the democratic forces led by <a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Governance and education index rankings of South Asian countries\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the UN cartographic section website disclaimers, "DESIGNATIONS USED: The depiction and use of boundaries, geographic names and related data shown on maps and included in lists, tables, documents, and databases on this web site are not warranted to be error free nor do they necessarily imply official endorsement or acceptance by the United Nations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unmapsworld_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-unmapsworld-12">[12]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFDoniger2010">Doniger 2010</a>, p.&#160;66: "Much of what we now call Hinduism may have had roots in cultures that thrived in South Asia long before the creation of textual evidence that we can decipher with any confidence. Remarkable cave paintings have been preserved from Mesolithic sites dating from c. 30,000 BCE in <a href="/wiki/Bhimbetka_rock_shelters" title="Bhimbetka rock shelters">Bhimbetka</a>, near present-day Bhopal, in the Vindhya Mountains in the province of Madhya Pradesh."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFJonesRyan2006">Jones &amp; Ryan 2006</a>, p.&#160;xvii: "Some practices of Hinduism must have originated in Neolithic times (c. 4000 BCE). The worship of certain plants and animals as sacred, for instance, could very likely have very great antiquity. The worship of goddesses, too, a part of Hinduism today, may be a feature that originated in the Neolithic."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Michaels: "They called themselves <i>arya</i> ("Aryans," literally "the hospitable," from the Vedic <i>arya</i>, "homey, the hospitable") but even in the Rgveda, <i>arya</i> denotes a cultural and linguistic boundary and not only a racial one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichaels200433_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichaels200433-90">[87]</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Citations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
